<div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. <span class=\"icon-newtab\">\n            </a></p>\n        </div>\n\n    <!-- End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" href=\"https://myiopscience.iop.org/signin?origin=a0&return=https%3A%2F%2Fiopscience.iop.org%2Fmyiopscience%2Falerts%2Fsubscribe%3FarticleID%3D0004-637X%2F866%2F1%2F65\"><span\n            class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">0004-637X/866/1/65</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n             <P>We present the discovery and measurements of a gravitationally lensed supernova (SN) behind the galaxy cluster MOO\u00a0J1014+0038. Based on multi-band <I>Hubble Space Telescope</I> and Very Large Telescope (VLT) photometry of the supernova, and VLT spectroscopy of the host galaxy, we find a 97.5% probability that this SN is a SN\u00a0Ia, and a 2.5% chance of a CC SN. Our typing algorithm combines the shape and color of the light curve with the expected rates of each SN type in the host galaxy. With a redshift of 2.2216, this is the highest redshift SN\u00a0Ia discovered with a spectroscopic host-galaxy redshift. A further distinguishing feature is that the lensing cluster, at redshift 1.23, is the most distant to date to have an amplified SN. The SN lies in the middle of the color and light-curve shape distributions found at lower redshift, disfavoring strong evolution to <I>z</I>\u00a0=\u00a02.22. We estimate an amplification due to gravitational lensing of <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"${2.8}_{-0.5}^{+0.6}$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/apjaad565ieqn1.gif\"></IMG> (1.10\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.23 mag)\u2014compatible with the value estimated from the weak-lensing-derived mass and the mass\u2013concentration relation from \u039bCDM simulations\u2014making it the most amplified SN\u00a0Ia discovered behind a galaxy cluster.</P> </div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start title=\"Export BibTex\">BibTeX</a>\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=0004-637X/866/1/65&doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aad565&exportFormat=iopexport_ris&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn href=\"/journal/0004-637X/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaad565s1\" name=\"apjaad565s1\">1.\u00a0Introduction</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Gravitational lensing by massive galaxy clusters offers an amplified and magnified view of the high-redshift universe. Several examples of supernovae (SNe) lensed by foreground clusters have been found in recent years (Goobar et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib32\">2009</a>; Amanullah et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib1\">2011</a>; Nordin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib65\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib65\">2014</a>; Patel et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib68\">2014</a>; Kelly et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib42\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib42\">2015</a>; Rodney et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib75\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib75\">2015a</a>; Petrushevska et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib69\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib69\">2016</a>). Four of these cluster-lensed SNe have been of Type\u00a0Ia (SNe Ia), from which the amplification due to lensing has been determined. (Two additional SNe Ia that were lensed by field galaxies have also been found [Quimby et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib71\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib71\">2014</a>; Goobar et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib31\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib31\">2017</a>]; we summarize all referenced SNe in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaad565t1\">1</a>.)</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaad565t1\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 1.</b>\u00a0\nOther High-redshift or Gravitationally Lensed SNe\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaad565t1\" (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib69\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib69\">2016</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">CAND-821</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">1.70</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Spec</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Cluster</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">0.18</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">4.3</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">IIn</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Amanullah et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib1\">2011</a>), Petrushevska et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib69\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib69\">2016</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">CAND-1392</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">0.94</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Spec</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Cluster</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">0.18</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">2.7</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">IIP</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Petrushevska et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib69\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib69\">2016</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">CAND-10658</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\n<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565ieqn3.gif\" alt=\"${0.94}_{-0.27}^{+0.07}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{0.94}_{-0.27}^{+0.07}</script></span></span>\n</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Spec</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Cluster</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">0.18</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">1.7</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">IIn</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Petrushevska et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib69\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib69\">2016</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">CAND-10662</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\n<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565ieqn4.gif\" alt=\"${1.03}_{-0.17}^{+0.20}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{1.03}_{-0.17}^{+0.20}</script></span></span>\n</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Spec</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Cluster</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">0.18</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">2.6</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">IIP</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Petrushevska et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib69\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib69\">2016</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">iPTF16geu</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">0.41</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Spec</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Field</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">0.22</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">52<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaad565t1fna\">a</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Ia</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Goobar et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib31\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib31\">2017</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">SCP16C03 (\"Joseph\")</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">2.22</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Spec</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Cluster</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">1.23</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">2.8</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Ia</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">This Work</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<p><strong>Note.</strong></p>\n<a name=\"apjaad565t1fna\" id=\"apjaad565t1fna\"></a><sup> a</sup>Multiple images; amplification is sum over all images.\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/suppdata/apjaad565t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aad565\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/suppdata/apjaad565t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>The uniquely precise standardization possible with SNe\u00a0Ia provides amplification information, breaking the so-called mass-sheet degeneracy that is problematic for most shear-based lensing models, and permits independent direct tests of cluster mass models obtained from galaxy lensing (Nordin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib65\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib65\">2014</a>; Patel et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib68\">2014</a>; Rodney et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib75\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib75\">2015a</a>). Lenses that produce multiple SN images provide additional model constraints (Kelly et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib43\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib43\">2016b</a>). To date, the redshifts of gravitationally lensed background SNe\u00a0Ia have been at <em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a01.39, a redshift range where even without lensing the complete (normal) SN\u00a0Ia population can be detected using single-orbit <em>HST</em> visits. In cases of stronger amplification of sources beyond the redshift reach of normal observations, tests of SN\u00a0Ia properties and rates over a larger look-back time become possible. Here we report the discovery of the most amplified SN\u00a0Ia behind a galaxy cluster ever found, with a spectroscopic host-galaxy redshift making it also the most distant.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaad565s2\" name=\"apjaad565s2\">2.\u00a0Discovery</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The Supernova Cosmology Project's \"See\u00a0Change\" program (PI: Perlmutter) monitored 12 massive galaxy clusters in the redshift range 1.13\u20131.75 using the <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> (<em>HST</em>) Wide Field Camera 3 (WFC3) with the goals of greatly expanding the range of the high-redshift SN\u00a0Ia Hubble diagram and accurately determining high-redshift cluster masses via weak lensing. We observed each cluster every 5 weeks for one orbit split between the UVIS <em>F</em>814<em>W</em>, the IR <em>F</em>105<em>W</em>, and the IR <em>F</em>140<em>W</em> filters. The supernova survey was very deep; our 50% completeness for simulated SN detection was AB 26.6 in <em>F</em>105<em>W</em>\u00a0+\u00a0<em>F</em>140<em>W</em> (B. Hayden et al. 2018, in preparation); this is ~1 mag fainter than a <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.75 SN\u00a0Ia at maximum.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaad565fn1\">19</a></sup>\n When a promising Type\u00a0Ia supernova candidate was found, at least one extra visit was triggered and executed within 2\u20133 observer-frame weeks after the initial discovery. These extra visits provided better light-curve sampling, usually close to maximum light, and frequently extended the wavelength range with the IR <em>F</em>160<em>W</em> filter.</p><p>On 2016 February\u00a029\u00a0UTC, we searched images of the <em>WISE</em>-selected (Wright et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib107\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib107\">2010</a>) massive galaxy cluster MOO\u00a0J1014+0038 (<em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.23, B. Decker et al. 2018, in preparation; <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565ieqn5.gif\" alt=\"${M}_{200}=(5.6\\pm 0.6)\\times {10}^{14}\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{M}_{200}=(5.6\\pm 0.6)\\times {10}^{14}\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>, Brodwin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib11\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib11\">2015</a>), from the Massive and Distant Clusters of <em>WISE</em> Survey (MaDCoWS; Gettings et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib28\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib28\">2012</a>; Stanford et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib92\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib92\">2014</a>; Gonzalez et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib30\">2015</a>). We detected a red (WFC3 <em>F</em>140<em>W</em>\u00a0=\u00a025.1, <em>F</em>105<em>W</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>F</em>140<em>W</em>\u00a0=1.4 AB mag; upper limit only in <em>F</em>814<em>W</em>) supernova at <em>\u03b1</em>\u00a0=\u00a0153<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />52655, <em>\u03b4</em>\u00a0=\u00a0+0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />64041 (J2000, aligned to USNO-B1). This SN was internally designated as SN\u00a0SCP16C03,<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaad565fn2\">20</a></sup>\n as it was the third SN found in this cluster field (alphabetically labeled cluster \"C\") in 2016. As shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaad565f1\">1</a>, the SN lies on a red galaxy having a color of <em>F</em>105<em>W</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>F</em>140<em>W</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.5 AB mag and is located 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />7 from the core of this galaxy (<em>\u03b1</em>\u00a0=\u00a0153<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />52643, <em>\u03b4</em>\u00a0=\u00a0+0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />64025). We conclude that this galaxy must be the host galaxy; there are no other galaxies nearby, the light curve is incompatible with those possible from an intra-cluster SN within MOO\u00a0J1014+0038 (as discussed in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaad565s6\">6</a>), and the probability of a chance projection is negligible (~0.2%, as discussed in Appendix <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaad565app2\">B</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaad565f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaad565f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565f1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565f1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0Color image of the central part of MOO\u00a0J1014+0038 made with an <em>F</em>814<em>W</em> stack and the <em>F</em>105<em>W</em> and <em>F</em>160<em>W</em> data from our first triggered <em>HST</em> imaging near maximum light. The inset panel uses different scaling, and incorporates only IR data (<em>F</em>105<em>W</em>, <em>F</em>125<em>W</em>, and <em>F</em>160<em>W</em>). The compass arrows are 1'' in linear scale. Both panels use hyperbolic arcsine intensity scaling. In green, we show contours of our computed lensing amplification model (in magnitudes), described in Section <a class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaad565s8\">8</a>.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaad565f1\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/downloadFigure/figure/apjaad565f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaad565f1\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaad565f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaad565s3\" name=\"apjaad565s3\">3.\u00a0Spectroscopic and Photometric Follow-up</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We activated ToO spectroscopic observations (PI: Hook) using X-shooter, the multi-wavelength medium resolution spectrograph on the Very Large Telescope (Vernet et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib104\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib104\">2011</a>). Five \"Observation Blocks\" were taken between 2016 March\u00a04\u20135 (UT), yielding a total integration time of 3.8, 4.4, and 5.0\u00a0hr in the X-shooter UVB, VIS, and NIR arms, respectively. Although the slit orientation captured both the host galaxy and the SN (shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaad565f2\">2</a>), the galaxy was ~4 mag brighter, so only a host-galaxy spectrum could be extracted. The data were reduced to wavelength- and flux-calibrated, sky-subtracted, 2D spectra using the Reflex software (Freudling et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib27\">2013</a>). Optimal 1D-extractions were determined using a combination of custom and <tt>IRAF</tt> (Tody <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib100\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib100\">1993</a>) routines.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaad565fn3\">21</a></sup>\n The extractions used a Gaussian profile in the cross-dispersion direction, the width of which was determined by fitting the trace in each (binned) 2D spectrum individually. These extractions were combined using the weighted mean to create a final 1D spectrum. We corrected for telluric absorption using a model atmosphere computed by the Line-by-Line Radiative Transfer Model (Clough et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib19\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib19\">1992</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib20\">2005</a>) retrieved through Telfit (Gullikson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib33\">2014</a>). Our observations were obtained at a low mean airmass of ~1.15 with a NIR slit width of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />9 (matching the mean seeing). The X-shooter NIR arm is aligned with the optical at 13100 \u00c5<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaad565fn4\">22</a></sup>\n; the atmospheric differential refraction over the NIR wavelength range for this airmass range is &lt;0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />1. For a Gaussian PSF (with FWHM 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />9) shifted by 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />1, the differential slit loss would be 2%. Thus, atmospheric differential refraction has a negligible impact on the calibration of our NIR spectrum. The host-galaxy spectrum is shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaad565f3\">3</a>. Balmer H<em>\u03b4</em> and H<em>\u03b2</em> absorption lines are clearly detected, as are the Ca\u00a0H&amp;K absorption lines. Mg\u00a0b is likely detected as well. These lines provide the main contribution to the weighted cross-correlation, as shown in the lower panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaad565f3\">3</a>, yielding a redshift of 2.2216\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0002 for the host galaxy. No emission lines were detected (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaad565s5-3\">5.3</a> for further details).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaad565f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaad565f2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565f2_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 2.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565f2_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 2.</strong>\u00a0Illustration of the X-shooter slit orientation and location on the SN and host galaxy.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaad565f2\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/downloadFigure/figure/apjaad565f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaad565f2\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaad565f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaad565f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaad565f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565f3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565f3_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0Top:\u00a0flux-calibrated, telluric corrected, de-lensed (by a factor of 2.8; see Section <a class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaad565s7\">7</a>), and binned (14 \u00c5 observer-frame) spectrum of the host galaxy (red line). Gray shaded regions indicate strong atmospheric absorption. The best-fit <tt>FAST</tt> model (fit to both the photometry and spectrum) is shown in black, convolved by the 305 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> velocity dispersion estimated by <tt>ppxf</tt>. Prominent features identified in both spectra are highlighted with light blue shading and labeled; the H<em>\u03b1</em> line is labeled for reference, but no prominent contribution to the cross-correlation is detected from it. Bottom:\u00a0the contribution to the weighted cross-correlation of each wavelength element of the spectrum. Regions of heavy atmospheric absorption are properly de-weighted, and the prominent features easily identified by eye provide a confident redshift determination of 2.2216\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0002.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaad565f3\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/downloadFigure/figure/apjaad565f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaad565f3\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaad565f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>This SN was 15'' away from the center of a dense concentration of cluster galaxies. Our initial flux amplification estimate was ~2.2 , calculated by assuming that the optical and halo center were the same, and employing a Navarro\u2013Frenk\u2013White dark matter profile (Navarro et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib63\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib63\">1997</a>). Based on the likelihood that this would turn out to be a highly magnified, high-redshift SN\u00a0Ia, we applied for Director's Discretionary time on <em>HST</em> and were granted a three-orbit disruptive ToO to ensure a good measurement of the SN SED. We triggered <em>F</em>105<em>W</em>, <em>F</em>125<em>W</em>, and <em>F</em>160<em>W</em> imaging from our \"See Change\" allocation. We did not request <em>HST</em> grism spectroscopy, as the roll angle range available would not have allowed for a clean separation of the SN and its host. In addition to our triggered follow-up, we obtained additional WFC3 <em>F</em>814<em>W</em>, <em>F</em>105<em>W</em>, and <em>F</em>140<em>W</em> imaging at two more previously scheduled orbits (the cadenced search visits for discovering SNe). We also were granted Director's Discretionary time on VLT for imaging in the <em>K</em><sub><em>s</em></sub> band (PI: Nordin) with HAWK-I (Kissler-Patig et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib46\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib46\">2008</a>) in order to extend the wavelength range redder than is possible with <em>HST</em>.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaad565s4\" name=\"apjaad565s4\">4.\u00a0SN Photometry</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>With a pixel size of ~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />128, the WFC3 IR channel undersamples the PSF, making it difficult to remove underlying galaxy light with image resampling and subtraction. In addition, this SN poses an unusual, but not unknown, challenge, as we have no reference (SN-free) images in <em>F</em>125<em>W</em> and <em>F</em>160<em>W</em>, necessitating interpolation of the galaxy light over the SN position. To meet these needs, we have developed a \"forward modeling\" code described in Suzuki et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib99\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib99\">2012</a>) and Rubin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib81\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib81\">2013</a>) and updated for WFC3 IR in Nordin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib65\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib65\">2014</a>). This code fits each pixel as observed (flat-fielded \"flt\" images for WFC3 IR, CTE-corrected, flat-fielded \"flc\" images for WFC3 UVIS)\u2014that is, without resampling due to spatial alignment or correction for distortion. It does this by creating an analytic model of the scene, convolving that model with the PSF, and fitting it to the pixel values. In all cases, the effect on the flatfield of pixel area variations over the FoV are taken into account in order to properly account for spatial distortion.</p><p>For the host galaxy, our analytic model is a linear sum of an azimuthally symmetric spline (a 1D, radially varying component that is allowed to have ellipticity) and a 2D grid to capture azimuthal asymmetries.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaad565fn5\">23</a></sup>\n To these splines, we include a model for a point source representing the SN, with a different fitted amplitude in each epoch. As there are reference images in the cadenced IR filters (<em>F</em>105<em>W</em> and <em>F</em>140<em>W</em>), these can be used as a cross-check of our ability to do photometry in <em>F</em>125<em>W</em> and <em>F</em>160<em>W</em>, for which references are lacking. We obtain nearly identical photometry in the <em>F</em>105<em>W</em> and <em>F</em>140<em>W</em> bands with and without modeling the reference images, although the uncertainties are smaller when including references. Testing with simulated SNe indicates no photometric biases at the 0.01 mag level, and accurate uncertainties,<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaad565fn6\">24</a></sup>\n even without using reference images.</p><p>There is only weak evidence for SN light in the <em>F</em>814<em>W</em> filter, as expected for such a high redshift SN\u00a0Ia. The low S/N necessitates a different treatment than the IR, where the offset between the SN and host galaxy was treated as a fit parameter. To determine the location of the SN in the <em>F</em>814<em>W</em> images, we start by aligning the UVIS and IR exposures using <tt>TweakReg</tt>,<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaad565fn7\">25</a></sup>\n and then drizzling to a common frame using <tt>AstroDrizzle</tt>. (These resampled images are not used for the SN photometry.) Then we perform PSF photometry on the UVIS images using the centroid transferred (using <tt>pixtopix</tt>) from that measured in the IR images, where the SN is detected. We fit for a spatially constant background underneath the SN, incorporating both the sky and underlying galaxy. Even the core of the galaxy is only detected at low S/N in each <em>F</em>814<em>W</em> exposure, so the second derivative<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaad565fn8\">26</a></sup>\n underneath the SN is small.</p><p>Bad weather allowed only one of the seven Hawk-I <em>K</em><sub><em>s</em></sub> observing blocks to be executed; 40 minutes of effective exposure time was obtained in excellent seeing (0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />27), enabling a measurement of the SN flux. We use the same host-galaxy model as for the WFC3 IR data, but with the offset of the SN from the host fixed, and employing field stars to derive the PSF. We determine the flux calibration (in AB mags) from the standard star FS19 and from the 2MASS (Skrutskie et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib91\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib91\">2006</a>) magnitudes of the field stars. Although the brightness uncertainty of 60% is too large to improve the distance measurements, the additional rest-frame <em>R</em>-band coverage helped with photometric classification.</p><p>We present the resulting SN photometry in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaad565t2\">2</a>. The uncertainty in the host-galaxy subtraction in each band leads to correlations between the WFC3 IR photometry measurements (in the data for each filter), so we also provide the inverse covariance matrix in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaad565t3\">3</a>. We take the WFC3 IR zeropoints from Nordin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib65\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib65\">2014</a>), converted to AB magnitudes, which take into account the WFC3 IR count-rate nonlinearity. For the UVIS F814W filter, we use the STScI-provided UVIS zeropoint, after correcting the encircled energy to an infinite aperture.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaad565t2\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 2.</b>\u00a0\nPhotometry for SN SCP16C03\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaad565t2\" photometric measurements. These data are correlated (within each band) due to uncertainty in the underlying host-galaxy light.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/suppdata/apjaad565t3_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aad565\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/suppdata/apjaad565t3_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaad565s5\" name=\"apjaad565s5\">5.\u00a0Host-galaxy Properties</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>In this section, we present our measurements of the host-galaxy properties from spectroscopy and imaging, and summarize the evidence that the galaxy is old for its redshift and therefore lacking significant star formation in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaad565s5-5\">5.5</a>.</p><h3 id=\"apjaad565s5-1\" name=\"apjaad565s5-1\">5.1.\u00a0Host-galaxy Photometry</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We perform photometry of the host galaxy on aligned, stacked (SN-free) images using <tt>SEP.</tt><sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaad565fn9\">27</a></sup>\n To minimize contamination by light from the nearby galaxies, we use an elliptical aperture set to 1.2 times the Kron radius (Kron <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib49\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib49\">1980</a>).<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaad565fn10\">28</a></sup>\n In addition to the <em>HST</em> WFC3 photometry, we use archival <em>Spitzer</em> IRAC CH1 and CH2 data (A. H. Gonzalez et al. 2018, in preparation), and we obtained bluer <em>g</em>', <em>r</em>', and <em>i</em>' photometry of the host with the OSIRIS instrument at the Gran Telescopio Canarias (GTC). We determine the zeropoints of this photometry using an SDSS star in the GTC field of view (both the star and galaxy are measured with the same elliptical aperture). We present the host-galaxy photometry in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaad565t4\">4</a>.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaad565t4\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 4.</b>\u00a0\nHost-galaxy Photometry\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaad565t4\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/suppdata/apjaad565t4_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 4\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\".\">20.79</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\".\">0.44</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Hawk-I</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" We scale to <em>\u03bc</em>Jy (AB zeropoint of 23.9).</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/suppdata/apjaad565t4_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aad565\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/866/1/65/suppdata/apjaad565t4_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div><h3 id=\"apjaad565s5-2\" name=\"apjaad565s5-2\">5.2.\u00a0Host Age, Star Formation Rate, and Mass from SED Fitting</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>While SED fitting to broadband photometry has a well-known degeneracy between age, dust, and metallicity (e.g., Bell &amp; de Jong <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib6\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib6\">2001</a>), the X-shooter spectrum has many absorption features that can help break that degeneracy. To simultaneously fit the spectrum and the photometry, we use <tt>FAST</tt> (Kriek et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib48\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib48\">2009</a>).</p><p>We calibrate the X-shooter spectrum to the de-lensed <em>HST</em> photometry in bands <em>F</em>125<em>W</em>, <em>F</em>140<em>W</em>, and <em>F</em>160<em>W</em> by integrating the de-lensed X-shooter spectrum over these filters; we find a multiplicative factor of 1.5 in flux is required to match the <em>HST</em>\u00a0photometry. We then bin the X-shooter spectrum to 5 \u00c5. We use the high-resolution stellar population synthesis models included with <tt>FAST</tt>, performing a fit using both Bruzual and Charlot (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib12\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib12\">2003</a>; BC03) and Conroy et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib22\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib22\">2009</a>; FSPS) models, and averaging the two results (they agree extremely well). We use the Chabrier IMF (Chabrier <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib16\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib16\">2003</a>), with a delayed-exponential star formation history and the default \"kc\" parameterization of the dust attenuation curve (Kriek &amp; Conroy <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib47\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib47\">2013</a>). We first fit to a coarse grid; then progressively fit to a finer grid near the best-fit region of parameter space to better estimate uncertainties. Note that <tt>FAST</tt> does not model emission lines. <tt>FAST</tt> returns a <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> of 1385 for 2182 degrees of freedom for the BC03 models, and <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> of 1414 for 2179 degrees of freedom using the FSPS models. The final uncertainties are estimated using the <tt>FAST</tt> Monte Carlo simulation option, sampling 1000 times. The best-fit model and derived parameters are presented in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaad565t5\">5</a>, and the model spectrum is shown overlaid on the X-shooter spectrum in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaad565f3\">3</a>; we show the model spectrum with the broadband photometry in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaad565f4\">4</a>. The best-fit composite-stellar-population template has an age of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565ieqn6.gif\" alt=\"$1.60\\pm 0.1$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1.60\\pm 0.1</script></span></span> Gyr; as the age of the universe at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.22 is only 2.96 Gyr, the implied formation redshift is <em>z</em><sub>form</sub>\u00a0~\u00a04.5. The galaxy is very massive, with a stellar mass of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565ieqn7.gif\" alt=\"$11.08\\pm 0.02$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">11.08\\pm 0.02</script></span></span> <em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>, and it has a low SFR of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565ieqn8.gif\" alt=\"$0.4\\pm 0.2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">0.4\\pm 0.2</script></span></span> <em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub> yr<sup>\u22121</sup> (averaged over the prior 30 Myr), given its mass. The <tt>FAST</tt> star formation history model indicates that 99.94% of all stars expected to ever form have already formed in this galaxy. <tt>FAST</tt> finds little dust, with a mean <em>A</em><sub><em>V</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a0<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565ieqn9.gif\" alt=\"$0.3\\pm 0.08$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">0.3\\pm 0.08</script></span></span>. We assume a two-component dust model of Charlot and Fall (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib17\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib17\">2000</a>), where the dust optical depth for older stars is 0.3 times the optical depth for young (i.e., &lt;10 Myr) stars. This implies <em>A</em><sub><em>V</em></sub>\u00a0~\u00a0<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/866/1/65/Full/apjaad565ieqn10.gif\" alt=\"$1.0\\,\\pm 0.27$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1.0\\,\\pm 0.27</script></span></span> mag for any young stellar component. The age measurement is sufficiently precise to contribute a cosmochronometry measurement and thereby help constrain cosmological parameters (e.g., Jimenez &amp; Loeb <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib38\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib38\">2002</a>; Stern et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib94\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib94\">2010</a>; Moresco et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaad565bib60\" id=\"fnref-apjaad565bib60\">2012</a>).</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaad565t5\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 5.</b>\u00a0\nSCP16C03 Host-galaxy
